  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b913bf34-d7e1-447f-a61a-2f4f0df9bc76'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer2530227017365000933">In a steam-filled diner in a college town, Flannery Jansen catches sight of something more beautiful than she's ever seen: a graduate student, reading.   <span id="freeText2530227017365000933" style="display:none">In a steam-filled diner in a college town, Flannery Jansen catches sight of something more beautiful than she's ever seen: a graduate student, reading. The seventeen-year-old, new to everything around her—college, the East Coast, bodies of literature, and the sexual flurries of student life—is shocked by her desire to follow this wherever it will take her. When Flannery finds herself enrolled in a class with the remote, brilliant older woman, she is intimidated at first, but gradually becomes Anne Arden's student—Baudelaire, lipstick colors, or how to travel with a lover—Flannery proves an eager pupil, until one day learns more about Anne than she ever wanted to know.</span>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_487921250" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/487921250" />
    <a title="April" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10478000-april"><img alt="April" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605047392p2/10478000.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/487921250?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="April" class="user" itemprop="url" name="April" href="/user/show/10478000-april">April</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10478000-april?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer487921250&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer487921250" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5810889770356019730">One word: lukewarm. <br/><br/>(Contains spoiler)<br/>Beautifully written, <i>Pages for You</i> could have been quite a brutally realistic romance crafted with the omniscient fluidity of Brownrigg's writing; sadly, it wasn't for me. Though given a charming narrative with particularly gorgeous scenes, I couldn't shake the fact that I absolutely hated the ending. It wasn't the fact that Anne ended up with the surprisingly perfecto Jasper who we learn 'had a place' in Anne all along that could not be filled by Flannery o</span>
  <span id="freeText5810889770356019730" style="display:none">One word: lukewarm. <br /><br />(Contains spoiler)<br />Beautifully written, <i>Pages for You</i> could have been quite a brutally realistic romance crafted with the omniscient fluidity of Brownrigg's writing; sadly, it wasn't for me. Though given a charming narrative with particularly gorgeous scenes, I couldn't shake the fact that I absolutely hated the ending. It wasn't the fact that Anne ended up with the surprisingly perfecto Jasper who we learn 'had a place' in Anne all along that could not be filled by Flannery or the fact that it lacked in spontaneity or was deprived of some sort of climactic voluptuous rendezvous, it was the fact that <i>it had to be a guy.</i> It irked me because I felt it perpetuated the common misconception that women merely lust for one another when a guy isn't around and then resume to some form of male worship when they get back. It annoyed me a lot and although the ending was respectably simplistic it completely ruined it for me. <br /><br />Another thing that I wasn't fond of: Flannery. Generally, I have this idea that there are some protagonists in Lit that <i>are</i> their story and there are others that are used <i>for</i> their story...and I felt Flan fell into the latter category. I didn't like her at all. After I finished the book I concluded merely that a) she was pretty and that b) she was in love with Anne. That was all. I understand that she was trying to 'find herself' but I would've liked her to have just a little bit more of a personality than just some pretty college girl who we know could have any guy she wants yet is (or is not?) a lesbian who seems to care little for anyone else but Anne. <br /><br />Brownrigg's writing is worth one of those 3 stars, nonetheless. Some scenes she transcribes in a kind of 'watercolour fashion' i.e, in a very delicately exquisite way. It's likely I'm just being really picky but I couldn't help noticing faults here and there (and hating myself for it at the same time). It's still quite a nicely told story and I did swoon over certain snippets (hehe). To prove it I'll finish with some of my favourite quotes/parts in the tale: <br /><br /><i>"I'd like to pay your palms the same favor that you pay these pages, searching them for grooves and images and the secret signs of hunger, as you may scan these words for hidden messages. The lines of your hand might be a guide to your gifts for pleasure, or a clue to where you'll take me, or a map of where I might take you."</i><br /><br /><i>"But sleeping: that was a new intimacy altogether and one Flannery often could not believe she shared. It was a secret, wasn't it? Sleeping? What a person looked like when they couldn't help it; what that defenselessness might suggest; what revelations might be conveyed by that loosened, floppy shape, in the unintended words or murmurs of the dreamer?"</i>*<br /><br /><i>"If she did believe in souls (maybe, who knew, it was something she'd have to grow up a little to form an opinion on), she would say that Anne's spoke to her through her eyes."</i>**<br /><br /><i>"It is an old story. One of the oldest. They would not have had to travel so far just to learn it: Lust—open, naked lust—must be named and punished. How else can we hope to keep the world in order?"</i> <br /><br />*I never did find that song 'about a woman who learns of her lover's infidelities from the endearments he speaks in his sleep.' If anyone knows I'd be thankful if they told me. <br />**Basically this whole paragraph about her eyes and how she could never describe them. I spent the whole section aww-ing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5810889770356019730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2067402026" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2067402026" />
    <a title="Julie Ehlers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2120450-julie-ehlers"><img alt="Julie Ehlers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1446217915p2/2120450.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2067402026?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Ehlers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Ehlers" href="/user/show/2120450-julie-ehlers">Julie Ehlers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2120450-julie-ehlers?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2067402026" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14673878632518326423">Sometimes I really want to write poetry, but I can't because I don't know anything about poetry. And then I think, "Maybe I should just write it as prose. You know, just not break it up into little short lines." As I was reading <i>Pages for You</i> it occurred to me that Sylvia Brownrigg had done something similar with this novel. The chapters are quite short, usually only about a page and a half; each chapter clearly has its own theme, and they make liberal use of metaphor, description, and idiom, ye</span>
  <span id="freeText14673878632518326423" style="display:none">Sometimes I really want to write poetry, but I can't because I don't know anything about poetry. And then I think, "Maybe I should just write it as prose. You know, just not break it up into little short lines." As I was reading <i>Pages for You</i> it occurred to me that Sylvia Brownrigg had done something similar with this novel. The chapters are quite short, usually only about a page and a half; each chapter clearly has its own theme, and they make liberal use of metaphor, description, and idiom, yet—as their short length would imply—with a certain amount of sparseness and economy.<br /><br />Recently I read Brownrigg's first novel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/952750814?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Metaphysical Touch</a>, and while I liked it fine, I found it a bit gimmicky, overdone, and overly long. <i>Pages for You</i> is its opposite, a simple girl-meets-girl, girl-gets-girl, girl-loses girl (not a spoiler; it's on the first page) story that succeeds on the authenticity of its emotions. Do you want to hear about the thrill of pursuit and seduction? The self-discovery that accompanies it? The rush of infatuation? The pain of heartbreak? If this all sounds OK to you, you might enjoy this poetic ode to being young and in love.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14673878632518326423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2652158092" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2652158092" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26682058-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602529501p2/26682058.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2652158092?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/26682058-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2652158092" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1251929116670585868"><i>"It wasn't that she <b>wanted</b> the coffee, no. That wasn't it. Rather, she wanted to <b>be</b> the coffee: she envied the dark drink its chance to taste those lips."</i> -- page 9<br/><br/>The first great book I've read this year (and we're only a week into it!), I'd like to thank my local library for recently obtaining a copy of <i>Pages For You</i> and prominently displaying it at their fiction shelves. I don't think I would have otherwise heard of this book and/or author Sylvia Brownrigg.<br/><br/>Apparently set just before the Inter</span>
  <span id="freeText1251929116670585868" style="display:none"><i>"It wasn't that she <b>wanted</b> the coffee, no. That wasn't it. Rather, she wanted to <b>be</b> the coffee: she envied the dark drink its chance to taste those lips."</i> -- page 9<br /><br />The first great book I've read this year (and we're only a week into it!), I'd like to thank my local library for recently obtaining a copy of <i>Pages For You</i> and prominently displaying it at their fiction shelves. I don't think I would have otherwise heard of this book and/or author Sylvia Brownrigg.<br /><br />Apparently set just before the Internet / cell-phone / LGBTQ acceptance era of the mid- to late 90's, <i>Pages</i> follows college freshman Flannery Jansen - a tall, blonde, slightly tomboyish small-town West Coast transplant - as she enters her first semester as an 'undeclared' student at a university in New England. Early on she stops for breakfast at a local diner and is thunderstruck by another patron during a brief 'meet cute' interaction. This is Anne Arden, a worldly-looking /-seeming twenty-eight year-old teaching assistant from the same university's literature department. (Anne is described as having cat-like green eyes, auburn hair, and a sly voice.) Flannery is immediately awed by Anne.<br /><br />During the autumn their paths cross repeatedly but platonically in and around campus until the Thanksgiving holiday break. Flannery composes a deeply romantic but mature and well-written poem for Anne (titled "Pages For You") to express her true feelings, and slips it to her as Anne departs for New York City by train. A day later, as Flannery is settling into a stretch of boredom, she receives a phone call from Anne - <i>"I think you'd better come to New York."</i> Cue the lightning strike!<br /><br />Sparks fly and fireworks explode as the relationship begins with the usual but joyous lust / love. (One chapter starts with <i>"The year's coldest days were the hottest she had ever lived."</i> Good Lord!) Very sensual and irresistible without being graphic, tawdry, or overly explicit, <i>Pages For You</i> was addictive reading as Brownrigg details the blossoming affair between Flannery and Anne during the school year. Written in short, spirited chapters, I was completely and immediately wrapped up in the story of these two women. That these characters also intelligently discuss and reference books, poetry, and writing - their shared common interests - in their conversations made said story all the better.<br /><br />But ultimately and unfortunately there is not a generic or standard story-book happy ending to the relationship. Some realistic problems, annoyances, and issues start to creep in and cause trouble, and I think (though some reviewers have disagreed) the book was stronger for going in this direction.<br /><br />This is not the type of book I usually read (but then neither was Patricia Highsmith's <i>The Price of Salt</i> and I loved that one, too) but I found that it simultaneously grabbed me by the heart while also hitting me in the gut <i>and</i> engaging my mind. There are not many fiction book that do that to me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1251929116670585868" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_82249732" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82249732" />
    <a title="Alsha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/977721-alsha"><img alt="Alsha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473723984p2/977721.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82249732?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alsha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alsha" href="/user/show/977721-alsha">Alsha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330484626" href="/book/show/471470.Pages_for_You">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alsha by: </span>
      Helen
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/977721-alsha?shelf=f-f">f-f</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82249732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9721004233495125491">The writing is pretentious and tries too hard to impress - I'm putting that out there from the start. But I also finished it over two evenings of reading, so there was a compelling pull to the underlying story as well. It probably says more about me than the book that I would have preferred a point of view from the 28 year old rather than the 17 year old. <br/><br/>It's divided into three sections - essentially 1) the build-up to the romance 2) the romance and 3) the decline of the romance. There were cer</span>
  <span id="freeText9721004233495125491" style="display:none">The writing is pretentious and tries too hard to impress - I'm putting that out there from the start. But I also finished it over two evenings of reading, so there was a compelling pull to the underlying story as well. It probably says more about me than the book that I would have preferred a point of view from the 28 year old rather than the 17 year old. <br /><br />It's divided into three sections - essentially 1) the build-up to the romance 2) the romance and 3) the decline of the romance. There were certainly areas of wonderful clarity and familiarity and I enjoyed the tension and awkwardness in the first part a great deal, but on principle I have a problem with narrative structure that's too transparent, in which the anatomy of the finale is known from the beginning. In this book, the reader knows from the first page that the relationship fails, so by the time I get to the third part of the story, there's no suspense, only a depressing denoument that has no twists and very little internal tension. Nothing happens; it just falls apart. If something had happened that forced a reinterpretation of the first page, I might have had a different reaction. At heart though, this novel is a portrait of the rise and fall of a relationship - simple - and that's a premise that both limits and frames the events within. If the quality of the writing and the insights had been better, this might have been exactly the type of lyrical prose I'd fall head over heels for. Just not this time. It didn't quite pull it off for me, and the characters didn't stick in my head either. <br /><br />The book definitely brought to mind the advantages of other genres though - if a relationship fails, it's not the end of the whole story (as it was here) - there's always plenty of other supporting or overriding plot to keep things going. Food for thought.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9721004233495125491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_207198096" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207198096" />
    <a title="P" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5602513-p"><img alt="P" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469378820p2/5602513.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207198096?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P" class="user" itemprop="url" name="P" href="/user/show/5602513-p">P</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330484626" href="/book/show/471470.Pages_for_You">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207198096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer783794823737157800"><p>Oh, where do I even start? This book is utterly amazing. Dare I even say that it's a masterpiece? I just love Brownrigg's style of writing, meticulous use of language and how she brings the sensuality of her words alive in this book. It's simply so refreshing to read. The plot, characters and pace were perfect (maybe partly because I can relate to Flannery and her feelings). I want to talk about them passionately, in more detail but I know that if I do, I won't stop, especially if I start with A</p></span>
  <span id="freeText783794823737157800" style="display:none"><p>Oh, where do I even start? This book is utterly amazing. Dare I even say that it's a masterpiece? I just love Brownrigg's style of writing, meticulous use of language and how she brings the sensuality of her words alive in this book. It's simply so refreshing to read. The plot, characters and pace were perfect (maybe partly because I can relate to Flannery and her feelings). I want to talk about them passionately, in more detail but I know that if I do, I won't stop, especially if I start with Anne Arden.</p><br /><p>I especially enjoyed the book's sense of humour. Also, I went through such a range of emotions while reading this book. Mostly I couldn't stop smiling while I read it and I honestly couldn't put it down! My heart ached deeply for the characters in the poignant parts of the book. I even remember cupping my hand over my mouth, gasping at a certain point and crying out, as if it would somehow prevent inevitable poignancy from occurring. There aren't many books that have moved me in the way that "Pages for You" has. I feel like my words aren't even adequate to explaining how amazing I think this book is. It's inexplicable.</p><br /><p>Brownrigg is definitely a very talented writer. Or maybe that's an understatement. I just feel so frustrated that I can't adequately voice how this book and her writing make me feel! I'm so glad and grateful for the existence of "Pages for You". It's a truly beautiful, unforgettable and unique book that I will always cherish. Thank you, Sylvia Brownrigg, thank you.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="783794823737157800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2246225673" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2246225673?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica Sullivan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica Sullivan" href="/user/show/1246157-jessica-sullivan">Jessica Sullivan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246157-jessica-sullivan?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1246157-jessica-sullivan?shelf=diverse-books">diverse-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2246225673" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1405127414006682462">I never felt fully immersed or deeply moved by this book, and I think I can pinpoint exactly why: the third-person narration kept me at a distance the whole time. How I wish I could have been deeper inside 17-year-old Flannery's head as she experienced first love with the poised and sophisticated Anne. Third-person narration just seemed like such a strange choice for this topic, and the intensity it was going for.<br/><br/>I didn't find myself savoring it, nor aching to read more. I knew going into it fro</span>
  <span id="freeText1405127414006682462" style="display:none">I never felt fully immersed or deeply moved by this book, and I think I can pinpoint exactly why: the third-person narration kept me at a distance the whole time. How I wish I could have been deeper inside 17-year-old Flannery's head as she experienced first love with the poised and sophisticated Anne. Third-person narration just seemed like such a strange choice for this topic, and the intensity it was going for.<br /><br />I didn't find myself savoring it, nor aching to read more. I knew going into it from reading others' reviews that it was going to have "pretentious" prose, but I'm typically the kind of person who enjoys that, so that wasn't necessarily the issue. (Though I wasn't entirely won over by the prose, which was borderline mawkish at times.) <br /><br />Criticism aside, this was a perfectly fine book. It propelled me along at a fast pace, it was totally readable. There was just something missing for me to transform it from a 3-star book into something deeply moving and unforgettable. I wanted to be wrecked by this but it just didn't happen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1405127414006682462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10257072336392460890">Flannery, a 17 year old college student, falls in love with Anne a lecturer at her university. Split into three sections this novel shows the longing, the affair, and the affair's decline. Sometimes overwritten, I was interested in these two characters, but it was just too much of the same: literature, lust, love. It became a very claustrophobic read, and not in a way that made me think that was clever - just a little irritating. </span>

<div id="review_2420867773" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2420867773" />
    <a title="Ana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1991298-ana"><img alt="Ana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528559847p2/1991298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2420867773?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ana" href="/user/show/1991298-ana">Ana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=kindle-scribd-library">kindle-scribd-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=eye-roll-worthy">eye-roll-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1991298-ana?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2420867773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4499449658463220833"><b>DNF @ 53%</b><br/><br/>I hadn’t heard of this book prior to the publication of its sequel, <i>Pages for Her</i>, and was surprised to find out that more than 15 years passed between the two novels. Since I was curious to read the recently released one, having loved <i>Call Me by Your Name</i>, with which they have similar plot points, I thought I’d start at the beginning. And, sadly, <b>end</b> there! <br/><br/>Pretentiously written with a rather retro vibe, as if from the 70s, where even the most lovely, tender moments are overblown by em</span>
  <span id="freeText4499449658463220833" style="display:none"><b>DNF @ 53%</b><br /><br />I hadn’t heard of this book prior to the publication of its sequel, <i>Pages for Her</i>, and was surprised to find out that more than 15 years passed between the two novels. Since I was curious to read the recently released one, having loved <i>Call Me by Your Name</i>, with which they have similar plot points, I thought I’d start at the beginning. And, sadly, <b>end</b> there! <br /><br />Pretentiously written with a rather retro vibe, as if from the 70s, where even the most lovely, tender moments are overblown by embellished prose or clichéd descriptions, <b>
  <i>Pages for You</i>
</b> is the sort of book I might have enjoyed if I were actually Flannery’s age. The two main characters felt really flat and the dialogue had me cringing every time Anne opened her mouth, with her rude pedantry. Halfway through, there’s little to no plot outside their relationship, and what we get is incredibly predictable, as if the writer is following a script, checking out points on a list. <br /><br />While the theory snob in me should be enjoying all the references to Susan Sontag and Benjamin’s <i>Reflections</i>, I think they only mask the lack of any substance. I was expecting something more from what is considered a ladies-loving-ladies classic. I know it is published in the early 2000s, but it still reads like melodramatic teen fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4499449658463220833" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3222024851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15618207561895624465">This is a devastatingly beautiful literary work, comparable in quality with Fiona Shaw's Tell It To the Bees. Emotionally, experiencing it is like gazing upon a magnificent painting. Brace yourself for this one, folks, but it's worth it. For fans of Abby Craden, this is a must-listen. She is at her finest here and it is apparent why she is considered one of the best narrators in the business. My heart is still feeling this - I don't think I'll shake it anytime soon.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18324953-gabie?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer559863337" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18046710657406575279">I’ve heard buzz about this book all over the place, good reviews at that, and feedback that it would “ruin my life.”<br/><br/>It did. In the most glorious way.<br/><br/>I seldom read romance novels but this one really exceeded my expectations. Brownrigg narrated it in such a poetic manner and in such a rich prose. Narrated from the point of view of a young Flannery, showing us a different side of relationships and allows us to reminisce on our firsts. Every word and item symbolizes something deeper than it original</span>
  <span id="freeText18046710657406575279" style="display:none">I’ve heard buzz about this book all over the place, good reviews at that, and feedback that it would “ruin my life.”<br /><br />It did. In the most glorious way.<br /><br />I seldom read romance novels but this one really exceeded my expectations. Brownrigg narrated it in such a poetic manner and in such a rich prose. Narrated from the point of view of a young Flannery, showing us a different side of relationships and allows us to reminisce on our firsts. Every word and item symbolizes something deeper than it originally appeared, affecting each character in such a significant way: the books, the emotions felt by both characters (more evidently Flannery’s) and the words spoken in their minds that never made it out of their mouths. Both characters affected and influenced each other in such an illustrious manner. Within the 3 parts of the book, we see a different Flannery, a different Anne (though she remains sexy the whole book like DAYUM). The little moments of bliss between the two lovers, like the make up game agh so cute and the little geeky talks they have about books and authors, made me love this book. Paying attention to the little things, cherishing and remembering them.<br /><br />The ending was quite rapid. It was kind of like, wait what just happened? Most everything in part 3 happened so fast because *spoiler* ok so Anne moved away and Flannery was alone for a while and she flew to her and they broke up because of a past love coming their way JUST. LIKE. THAT. I know it’s pretty cliche to say that I wanted them to stay together though, in the back of my mind, I didn’t think it would last because of the age gap and their differences but why end it like that?! Although I like the part when they were laying together and that Anne was feeling so much love for her still but not love love cry. <br /><br />The part after the break up scene has to be my favorite. Flannery walking through the campus, as she did before the love, before the heartbreak, before Anne. It was a new beginning for Flannery: the experienced, bruised and battered Flannery. She had grown but not entirely changed.<br /><br />I give this book a 8/10<br /><br />★★★★★★★★☆☆</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3577309677" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3577309677" />
    <a title="Niki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57137850-niki"><img alt="Niki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466915870p2/57137850.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3577309677?book_show_action=true">Oct 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niki" href="/user/show/57137850-niki">Niki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57137850-niki?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57137850-niki?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/57137850-niki?shelf=hard-pass">hard-pass</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3577309677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2102043642435221177">I'm gonna be honest, I came to this book looking for a second <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36336078.Call_Me_By_Your_Name__Call_Me_By_Your_Name___1_' title='Call Me By Your Name (Call Me By Your Name, #1) by André Aciman' rel='nofollow noopener'>Call Me By Your Name</a>, only this would be even better because it's women: an intoxicating, passionate, same-sex story between two people (with an age difference thrown into the mix, which is cause for a side-eye from me if I'm being honest). I didn't completely love CMBYN for several reasons, but it was a mesmerizing romance/ infatuation story and I wanted to read something similar.<br/><br/>Imagine my surprise and obvious disappointment when wh</span>
  <span id="freeText2102043642435221177" style="display:none">I'm gonna be honest, I came to this book looking for a second <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36336078.Call_Me_By_Your_Name__Call_Me_By_Your_Name___1_" title="Call Me By Your Name (Call Me By Your Name, #1) by André Aciman" rel="nofollow noopener">Call Me By Your Name</a>, only this would be even better because it's women: an intoxicating, passionate, same-sex story between two people (with an age difference thrown into the mix, which is cause for a side-eye from me if I'm being honest). I didn't completely love CMBYN for several reasons, but it was a mesmerizing romance/ infatuation story and I wanted to read something similar.<br /><br />Imagine my surprise and obvious disappointment when what I got instead was a clinical, immature, imbalanced and cringe-worthy "romance" with a stupid ending, to boot. I never, ever, ever felt ANY kind of chemistry or connection between Flannery and Anne. The relationship would obviously never be balanced between them anyway, but I wanted to feel the crush, the infatuation on Flannery's part, the despair of wanting to be in Anne's world and never fitting in, SOMETHING instead of cringe-worthy "I'm having SEX! I'm a WOMAN now! I have a LOVER! What am I going to call my LOVER, "darling" or "honey" or what?" And then pages and pages about just how cultured and better than everyone else Anne is.<br /><br />Almost every review I've seen praises the writing in particular, and I honestly don't get it. I didn't like the writing an any point, I never wanted to highlight a passage, share it with anyone, or even just stop and say "....Whoa" at any point. I didn't feel anything about it, and in a story about love and passion, I should have had. The only slightly better-written scenes were ones of anger and bitterness, and that's NOT where the great writing should have been in a story about a love affair.<br /><br />The characters were cardboard cutouts and never had any development or character traits besides "Flannery is soooo cute in her innocence, and Anne is so cultured and mysterious". I'm honestly not sure how many of the author's choices were actually on-purpose genius ones or simple incompetence, because on one hand, I think the entire story is supposed to be Flannery writing about it years after, so everything is her own POV and how she saw things (meaning: immaturely and firmly one-sided), but that still doesn't make the clinical writing and complete lack of passion and connection enjoyable to read about.<br /><br />I personally didn't care about the (stupid) ending, because by that point I didn't care about the book at all. It was just another reason to dislike it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2102043642435221177" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText17335553042151241247" style="display:none">The book concerns the convincing love affair between two women (the main character has been shrunk by the word Lesbian, and I agree) overshadowed by the coming-of-age and the coined word: "education" in terms of the university atmosphere and the education a woman could gain from the relationship, both falling in and out. <br /><br />The main character Flannery, fresh from the high school to the university, falls into the greenish eyes of the most beautiful woman she first saw at the diner without knowing she would become her TA.   <span id="freeText15530818569602697500" style="display:none">This is the story of someone who fell in love, not only with another human being, but also with herself. This is a self-discovery journey, a journey that teaches that with wonder comes loss, and that with sadness comes happiness. There are ups and downs, there are smiles and tears. In the end? It will be worth it. No matter how much it seems to hurt at the beginning, there will come a time in life when you will sit and smile at the memories from the moments that broke you into thousands of different tiny pieces. Those moments, those memories, those pieces... they are whoever you have become.<br /><br />This book is just beautiful. You too fall in love, you too start reading the signs... and they will break you... into tears, into smiles... What else could you really ask for?<br /><br />Still don't think that 17 is the appropriate age for Flannery, but reading this book was an absolute pleasure.</span>

<div id="review_2670643481" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2670643481" />
    <a title="Malum" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68337677-malum"><img alt="Malum" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518964187p2/68337677.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2670643481?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Malum" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Malum" href="/user/show/68337677-malum">Malum</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68337677-malum?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68337677-malum?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2670643481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12211657858022333689"><i>Pages for You</i> is like a cross between Alain de Botton's <i>Essays in Love</i> and Ann Bannon's <i>Odd Girl Out</i>. Like Botton's novel, it examines the life of a relationship through all of its twists and turns (although in a much less clinical way). And, like Bannon's pulp novel, it is about an experienced college girl and a naïve freshmen finding love together in a world that doesn't accept them <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[and also ends with a tragic "Oops, I guess I'm not a lesbian after all. Sorry!" moment <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoi</a></span></span>
  <span id="freeText12211657858022333689" style="display:none"><i>Pages for You</i> is like a cross between Alain de Botton's <i>Essays in Love</i> and Ann Bannon's <i>Odd Girl Out</i>. Like Botton's novel, it examines the life of a relationship through all of its twists and turns (although in a much less clinical way). And, like Bannon's pulp novel, it is about an experienced college girl and a naïve freshmen finding love together in a world that doesn't accept them <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and also ends with a tragic "Oops, I guess I'm not a lesbian after all. Sorry!" moment <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />This is a beautifully written novel that is about as close to poetry as you can get while still being prose. Where it loses points from me is that it just slightly overstays its welcome (do we really need to read about everything these women do, eat, read, and listen to? Every trip, every restaurant, every glance, every touch, and every conversation seems cataloged here, chapter after chapter).<br /><br />I saw that Brownrigg wrote a sequel to this novel but, after finishing this one, I can't help but feel that everything that needed to be said about these two women has been said.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12211657858022333689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2036478350" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2036478350" />
    <a title="Anna Baillie-Karas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11612758-anna-baillie-karas"><img alt="Anna Baillie-Karas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473347949p2/11612758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2036478350?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Baillie-Karas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Baillie-Karas" href="/user/show/11612758-anna-baillie-karas">Anna Baillie-Karas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2036478350" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6378072769912292092">Flannery, a university student, falls in love with Anne, 10 yrs her senior. This starts beautifully & the language is poetic & sensual throughout. Flannery & Anne are interesting, each strong in their own way, & the dynamics of a relationship wonderfully observed. But I didn’t share Flannery’s absorption in her new love. She was like a precocious uni student; it didn’t quite hold my interest. Saved by the lyrical writing.</span>
  <span id="freeText6378072769912292092" style="display:none">Flannery, a university student, falls in love with Anne, 10 yrs her senior. This starts beautifully &amp; the language is poetic &amp; sensual throughout. Flannery &amp; Anne are interesting, each strong in their own way, &amp; the dynamics of a relationship wonderfully observed. But I didn’t share Flannery’s absorption in her new love. She was like a precocious uni student; it didn’t quite hold my interest. Saved by the lyrical writing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6378072769912292092" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10697179-mel?shelf=owned">owned</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2086614783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2519900115245749954">I've got a new project on the go where I reorganized the TBR books on my shelf in a random order onto my shelves and I'm reading them in order. This was the next book to pop up, and I am so happy that it did. <br/><br/>This book follows Flannery Jansen, who at the start of her University life at the age of 17, falls in love at first sight with another woman and thus begins a very whirlwind romance. <br/><br/>I saw so much of myself in Flannery and therefore really enjoyed this. I read through this book in around 24</span>
  <span id="freeText2519900115245749954" style="display:none">I've got a new project on the go where I reorganized the TBR books on my shelf in a random order onto my shelves and I'm reading them in order. This was the next book to pop up, and I am so happy that it did. <br /><br />This book follows Flannery Jansen, who at the start of her University life at the age of 17, falls in love at first sight with another woman and thus begins a very whirlwind romance. <br /><br />I saw so much of myself in Flannery and therefore really enjoyed this. I read through this book in around 24 hours, and it was just a very poetic and beautiful reading experience. The author was able to manipulate my feelings and anytime she said I should feel or believe something, I did. Using a cross between a third and first person narrative, the writing was poetic and flowed. Each chapter was only 1 page and it made reading it a lot easier and smoother. I basically just threw myself into the book and let the characters and writing guide me through the story. <br /><br />This book was originally published in 2001 and has had a reprint because Brownrigg has released a sequel 17 years later that follows Flannery and Anne 20 years after the event of this first book. I initially held off ordering that sequel until I read this one, but I look forward to seeing where the lives of these two women has led and how this love story impacted them over time.<br />I relate heavily to Flannery's character and her situation in the book and I am curious to see what 20 years later looks like for her, and if maybe that is the same direction my life will go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2519900115245749954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_177336074" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177336074" />
    <a title="Liralen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4089241-liralen"><img alt="Liralen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294532488p2/4089241.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177336074?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liralen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liralen" href="/user/show/4089241-liralen">Liralen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089241-liralen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089241-liralen?shelf=z-2017">z-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089241-liralen?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089241-liralen?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177336074" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5878858519990821680">I wish I'd read this ten years ago—not because I think I particularly needed it ten years ago, but because there are ten years between Anne and Flannery, and I wonder whether I might have taken the book differently if I'd read it when I was at Flannery's age (seventeen, then eighteen) rather than Anne's (twenty-eight, as I am now).<br/><br/>I wish, too, that I hadn't read any reviews immediately before starting the book, because I also wonder whether I might have taken things differently had I not had an </span>
  <span id="freeText5878858519990821680" style="display:none">I wish I'd read this ten years ago—not because I think I particularly needed it ten years ago, but because there are ten years between Anne and Flannery, and I wonder whether I might have taken the book differently if I'd read it when I was at Flannery's age (seventeen, then eighteen) rather than Anne's (twenty-eight, as I am now).<br /><br />I wish, too, that I hadn't read any reviews immediately before starting the book, because I also wonder whether I might have taken things differently had I not had an inkling what was coming. (So, to anyone thinking about reading the book, take that as a warning...)<br /><br />As it is, I'm not sure. I couldn't really sympathise with Anne because I never quite trusted her—her motives, her love, her...reserve, I guess. And as I said above, I'm now the age she is in the book, and I'd <i>never</i> get involved with a seventeen-year-old, because at that age a ten-year difference is <i>massive</i>. That too made me reluctant to trust her. Meanwhile, I couldn't really sympathise with Flannery, either. Oh, I envy her for <i>going</i> for it, for figuring out what she wants and (eventually) doing something about it. Yet she falls so completely head over heels that I just couldn't relate. One thing to have a crush on somebody and another thing to structure your whole life around that crush, you know? She grows somewhat as the book goes on, and I suspect that as an older character she'd just get more interesting (oddly enough, it looks like there's a sequel planned to come out this summer), but oh gosh she's young.<br /><br />The writing is at times beautiful. It took me a little while to get into it, but I'm glad I kept going. I wish I knew when it was set—it was published in 2001, but was it meant to be contemporary? Or older? Because Flannery seems to be able to both buy alcohol and rent a car despite her young age, which I don't think was possible in the relevant states in 2001. Yet the relative lack of homophobia in the book makes me think it's not so likely to be set too far back... (Actually, that was another thing I appreciated—that the conflict really didn't come from the outside world but rather from Anne and Flannery.)<br /><br />Not sure I'll read the follow-up book when it comes out, but...I suspect curiosity will get me there eventually.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5878858519990821680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229740362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3993101803622974896">This book was delicious. The love scenes were not erotic per se but you would get right up there and cuts off right at the porn, but the writer did it right, it add to the erotic nature instead of taking away. The ending was heartbreaking and tragic and I cried. Yup this book made me slightly emotional at times.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YkXialhXg9HSX27a0+JoPv3JlTrwXTUvzO3kDyqJ4CygyI/pFs9bf1RU9rDMxVZ+mBa0MLEgfTh2Hwu0YGs+qQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AHnYj+be3CVCce8eoi2NXJzrjU0holaY2/pnyowuCFrC9LUMqEYEi8R6d3S9CrMc+TSsR2DfHo9hCIhxxszW3w==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6028735913891964657">Sylvia Brownrigg is the author of six books of fiction, including the novels <i>Pages for You</i> and <i>The Delivery Room</i>. Her most recent novel, <i>Pages for Her</i>, was published in July 2017 by Counterpoint in the US and Picador in the UK. <br/><br/>Sylvia's work has been included on the <i>NY Times</i> Notable list and the <i>LA Times</i> Best Books of the Year. Her reviews have appeared in the <i>NY Times</i>, <i>The Guardian</i>, and the <i>TLS</i>, </span>
  <span id="freeText6028735913891964657" style="display:none">Sylvia Brownrigg is the author of six books of fiction, including the novels <i>Pages for You</i> and <i>The Delivery Room</i>. Her most recent novel, <i>Pages for Her</i>, was published in July 2017 by Counterpoint in the US and Picador in the UK. <br /><br />Sylvia's work has been included on the <i>NY Times</i> Notable list and the <i>LA Times</i> Best Books of the Year. Her reviews have appeared in the <i>NY Times</i>, <i>The Guardian</i>, and the <i>TLS</i>, and she has taught at the American University in Paris. Her novel for children, <i>Kepler’s Dream</i> (published under the name Juliet Bell), has been turned into an independent feature film. <br /><br />She lives in Berkeley, CA, with her family, and continues to spend time in London. <br /></span>

<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32332878-pages-for-her"><img alt="Pages for Her" style="height: 75px;" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1495230816l/32332878._SY75_.jpg" />

<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_32332878'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32332878-pages-for-her?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Pages for Her<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/71922.Sylvia_Brownrigg?origin=series_works\">Sylvia Brownrigg<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"><\/span><\/span> 3.74 avg rating &mdash; 1,015 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2017\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer17855585006706071971\">Pages for Her is the story of two women, Flannery and Anne, each at a personal turning point, and the circumstances that lead to their reunion. Twenty years after their brief but passionate affair, chronicled in Brownrigg’s earlier novel Pages for Yo<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17855585006706071971\" style=\"display:none\">Pages for Her is the story of two women, Flannery and Anne, each at a personal turning point, and the circumstances that lead to their reunion. Twenty years after their brief but passionate affair, chronicled in Brownrigg’s earlier novel Pages for You, Flannery has the chance once again to meet Anne, who opened young Flannery up to the possibility of love—then left her heartbroken.Having long ago put their love behind them, they live now on opposite coasts. Anne has been in a deep, childless partnership with a fellow scholar Jasper, who recently left her. Flannery, to her own surprise, married a charismatic artist named Charles, with whom she has a young daughter. Submerged by her husband’s demands and personality and her adjustment to motherhood, Flannery has lost sight of her self and her work. When the two women meet at a conference, they find that the passion and understanding between them has endured, though it has been hidden. In rediscovering each other, they are able to rediscover themselves.Pages for Her is an exhilarating, passionate work that explores marriage, sexuality, and the transformative power of love over time.\n\nAdvance Praise for Pages for Her\n\n“[Sylvia Brownrigg] approaches her characters with clarity and sensitivity, capturing the nuances in the women\'s relationships to the people they love—as mother, daughter, sister, friend, wife, or lover—and the power they give those people to define and inspire them. . . . Brownrigg considers motherhood, romance, identity, and the changes brought by time in this tender, insightful novel.” —Kirkus Reviews (Starred Review!)\n\n“With Pages for Her, Sylvia Brownrigg has achieved the seemingly impossible, a gorgeous and piercing book that is both a huge gift to the many readers who loved its predecessor Pages for You and an exquisitely intelligent stand-alone novel about the intertwined arcs of time and love.” —Ann Packer, New York Times bestselling author of The Children’s Crusade\n\n“Sylvia Brownrigg’s Pages for Her is a complex portrait of two women\'s sexuality. In the romantic universe of Brownrigg’s novel, there is no either/or, no simple black and white. When characters—read people—are freed from the often blinding forces of personal obligation and private loss, a lust for intimacy takes over. In Pages for Her, Brownrigg gives us two accomplished women who, coming together after decades apart, understand that truth laid bare is best beguiled.” —Alice Sebold, author of The Almost Moon and The Lovely Bones\n\n“With Pages for Her, Brownrigg does open-heart surgery, probing the deep chamber where unfinished love resides, untouchable by time, still beating.” —Carol Anshaw, author of Carry the One\n\n“In this intense, compelling novel, Sylvia Brownrigg writes vividly about passion rekindled in midlife with the force of a tsunami. Pages for Her, the sequel to Pages for You, stands as a beautiful testament to human complexity, reminding us that fierce love comes in many forms, none of them mutually exclusive.” —Claire Messud, author of The Burning Girl \n\n“Pages for Her takes on all the Big Questions in women’s lives: what it means to have ‘enough’ in love, sex, work, motherhood; what we deserve; what we long for; how we get trapped; how we can break free. I found myself reading with pen in hand, compelled to underline both Brownrigg’s gorgeous prose and her astute insights.” —Peggy Orenstein, author of Girls &amp; Sex: Navigating the Complicated New Landscape \n\n“In elegant, graceful prose, Sylvia Brownrigg glides in and out of the lives of two women: Flannery, a writer married to a bombastic artist who values her beauty more than her mind; and Anne, an academic nearly a decade older whose decision not to have a child ends to her long-term relationship. Many years ago, these women shared a once-in-a-lifetime passion. Now, brought together serendipitously, they are surprised to discover [find] that time has done little to squelch [tamp down] desire. Nuanced, assured, and razor-sharp, Pages for Her is both a bittersweet story about rekindled love and a profound meditation on what it means to be alive.” —Christina Baker Kline, New York Times           <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Such nights are possible, and we survive them. It is a matter of sleeping next to the adored body you no longer have the right or inclination to love. Whether you are the one who casts off, or are the cast of yourself; whether your arms are the recoilers, or the ones that reach wantingly, then pull back, remembering they are no longer wanted. Two bodies that are used to each other's rhythms and sleep sounds, that know the turnings and breathings, know not to worry about that cough or that brief garbled grunt, that wildly flung arm or that stone-cold foot. Bodies that soon will not know each other's night selves: will touch each other through jackets and jeans and the cooled-down air of reestablished acquaintance, if such a thing is possible between a given pair of ex-lovers.&rdquo;</span>

This partial loads on almost every page view.  The associated React component makes
a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.
This is determined by how many signed out pagehits the user has executed an how recently they have
last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
